895 <section id="_67">

896

897 <h2>

898General Information About Melanoma</h2>

899

900 <div id="_section_67" class="pdq-sections">

901<div class="pdq-hp-patient-toggle">

902<a href="/types/skin/hp/melanoma-treatment-pdq">

903Go to Health Professional Version</a>

904</div>

905<div class="key-points">

906<h3 id="_67_kpBoxHdr" do-not-show="toc">

907Key Points</h3>

908<div id="_kp_section_67_1">

909<ul>

910<li>

911Melanoma is a disease in which malignant (cancer) cells form in melanocytes (cells that color the skin). </li>

912<li>

913There are different types of cancer that start in the skin.</li>

914<li>

915Melanoma can occur anywhere on the skin. </li>

916<li>

917Unusual moles, exposure to sunlight, and health history can

918 affect the risk of melanoma.</li>

919<li>

920Signs of melanoma include a change in the way a mole or pigmented area looks. </li>

921<li>

922Tests that examine the skin are used to diagnose melanoma.</li>

923<li>

924Certain factors affect prognosis (chance of recovery) and treatment options.</li>

925</ul>

926</div>

927</div>

928<section id="_68">

929<h3 id="_69" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

930Melanoma is a disease in which malignant (cancer) cells form in melanocytes (cells that color the skin). </h3>

931<p id="_70" tabindex="-1">

932The skin is the body&#8217;s largest <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=257523&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000257523&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

933organ</a>

934. It protects against heat, sunlight, injury, and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45364&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045364&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

935infection</a>

936. Skin also helps control body temperature and stores water, fat, and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=427253&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000427253&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

937vitamin D</a>

938. The skin has several layers, but the two main layers are the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46418&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046418&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

939epidermis</a>

940 (upper or outer layer) and the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46454&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046454&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

941dermis</a>

942 (lower or inner layer). <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=445084&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000445084&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

943Skin cancer</a>

944 begins in the epidermis, which is made up of three kinds of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

945cells</a>

946: </p>

947<div class="pdq-content-list">

948<ul id="_308">

949<li>

950<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46056&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046056&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

951Squamous cells</a>

952: Thin, flat cells that form the top layer of the epidermis.</li>

953<li>

954<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46516&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046516&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

955Basal cells</a>

956: Round cells under the squamous cells.</li>

957<li>

958<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46292&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046292&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

959Melanocytes</a>

960: Cells that make <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46291&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046291&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

961melanin</a>

962 and are found in the lower part of the epidermis. Melanin is the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46225&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046225&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

963pigment</a>

964 that gives skin its natural color. When skin is exposed to the sun or artificial light, melanocytes make more pigment and cause the skin to darken.</li>

965</ul>

966</div>

967<p id="_315" tabindex="-1">

968From 2010 to 2019, the number of new cases of melanoma increased by about 1% per year, though the number of deaths each year from melanoma continues to decrease. Melanoma is most common in adults, but it is sometimes found in children and

969 adolescents. For more information, see <a href="/types/skin/patient/child-melanoma-treatment-pdq">

970Childhood Melanoma Treatment</a>

971.</p>

972<figure id="figure_241" class="image-center">

973<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/579033.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

974Enlarge</a>

975<img id="_241" alt="Anatomy of the skin with melanocytes; drawing shows normal skin anatomy, including the epidermis, dermis, hair follicles, sweat glands, hair shafts, veins, arteries, fatty tissue, nerves, lymph vessels, oil glands, and subcutaneous tissue. The pullout shows a close-up of the squamous cell and basal cell layers of the epidermis above the dermis with blood vessels. Melanin is shown in the cells. A melanocyte is shown in the layer of basal cells at the deepest part of the epidermis." title="Anatomy of the skin with melanocytes; drawing shows normal skin anatomy, including the epidermis, dermis, hair follicles, sweat glands, hair shafts, veins, arteries, fatty tissue, nerves, lymph vessels, oil glands, and subcutaneous tissue. The pullout shows a close-up of the squamous cell and basal cell layers of the epidermis above the dermis with blood vessels. Melanin is shown in the cells. A melanocyte is shown in the layer of basal cells at the deepest part of the epidermis." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/579033-750.jpg">

976<figcaption class="caption-container">

977Anatomy of the skin, showing the epidermis, dermis, and subcutaneous tissue. Melanocytes are in the layer of basal cells at the deepest part of the epidermis.</figcaption>

978</figure>

979</section>

980<section id="_309">

981<h3 id="_310" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

982There are different types of cancer that start in the skin.</h3>

983<p id="_323" tabindex="-1">

984There are two main forms of skin cancer: melanoma and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46261&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046261&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

985nonmelanoma</a>

986.</p>

987<p id="_311" tabindex="-1">

988Melanoma is a rare form of skin cancer. It is more likely to invade nearby <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

989tissues</a>

990 and spread to other parts of the body than other types of skin cancer. When melanoma starts in the skin, it is called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46112&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046112&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

991cutaneous</a>

992 melanoma. Melanoma may also occur in <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=257212&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000257212&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

993mucous membranes</a>

994 (thin, moist layers of tissue that cover surfaces such as the lips). This summary is about cutaneous (skin) melanoma and melanoma that affects the mucous membranes.</p>

995<p id="_313" tabindex="-1">

996The most common types of skin cancer are <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46515&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046515&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

997basal cell carcinoma</a>

998 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46595&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046595&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

999squamous cell carcinoma</a>

1000. They are nonmelanoma skin cancers. Nonmelanoma skin cancers rarely spread to other parts of the body. For more information, see <a href="/types/skin/patient/skin-treatment-pdq">

1001Skin Cancer Treatment</a>

1002.</p>

1003</section>

1004<section id="_76">

1005<h3 id="_77" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1006Melanoma can occur anywhere on the skin. </h3>

1007<p id="_78" tabindex="-1">

1008In men,

1009 melanoma is often found on the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=796908&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000796908&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1010trunk</a>

1011 (the area from the shoulders to the hips)

1012 or the head and neck. In women, melanoma forms most often on the arms and legs.

1013 </p>

1014<p id="_314" tabindex="-1">

1015When melanoma occurs in the eye, it is called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269460&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269460&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1016intraocular</a>

1017 or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269467&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269467&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1018ocular melanoma</a>

1019. For more information, see <a href="/types/eye/patient/intraocular-melanoma-treatment-pdq">

1020Intraocular (Uveal) Melanoma Treatment</a>

1021.</p>

1022</section>

1023<section id="_79">

1024<h3 id="_80" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1025Unusual moles, exposure to sunlight, and health history can

1026 affect the risk of melanoma.</h3>

1027<p id="_81" tabindex="-1">

1028Anything that increases a person's chance of getting a disease is called a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45873&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045873&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1029risk factor</a>

1030. Not every person with one or more of these risk factors will develop melanoma, and it will develop in some people who don't have any known risk factors. Talk with your doctor if you think you may be at risk.</p>

1031<p id="_322" tabindex="-1">

1032Risk factors for melanoma include the

1033 following:</p>

1034<div class="pdq-content-list">

1035<ul id="_261">

1036<li>

1037Having a fair complexion, which includes the following:

1038<div class="pdq-content-list">

1039<ul id="_262" class="list-dash">

1040<li>

1041Fair skin that freckles and burns easily, does not tan, or tans poorly.

1042</li>

1043<li>

1044Blue or green or other light-colored eyes.

1045</li>

1046<li>

1047Red or blond hair.

1048</li>

1049</ul>

1050</div>

1051</li>

1052<li>

1053Being exposed to natural sunlight or artificial sunlight (such as from tanning beds).</li>

1054<li>

1055Being exposed to certain factors in the environment (in the air, your home or workplace, and your food and water). Some of the environmental risk factors for melanoma are <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45072&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045072&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1056radiation</a>

1057, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=463162&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000463162&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1058solvents</a>

1059, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46648&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046648&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1060vinyl chloride</a>

1061, and PCBs. </li>

1062<li>

1063Having a history of many blistering sunburns, especially as a child or teenager.

1064</li>

1065<li>

1066Having several large or many small <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46286&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046286&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1067moles</a>

1068.</li>

1069<li>

1070Having a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=302456&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000302456&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1071family history</a>

1072 of unusual moles (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=715624&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000715624&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1073atypical nevus</a>

1074 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45090&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045090&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1075syndrome</a>

1076).

1077</li>

1078<li>

1079Having a family or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=642021&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000642021&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1080personal history</a>

1081 of melanoma.

1082</li>

1083<li>

1084Being White.

1085</li>

1086<li>

1087Having a weakened <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46356&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046356&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1088immune system</a>

1089.</li>

1090<li>

1091Having certain changes in the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45693&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045693&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1092genes</a>

1093 that are linked to melanoma.</li>

1094</ul>

1095</div>

1096<p id="_295" tabindex="-1">

1097Being White or having a fair complexion increases the risk of melanoma, but anyone can have melanoma, including people with dark skin. </p>

1098<p id="_304" tabindex="-1">

1099For more information on risk factors for melanoma, see the following:</p>

1100<div class="pdq-content-list">

1102<li>

1104Genetics of Skin Cancer</a>

1106<li>

1113<section id="_83">

1114<h3 id="_84" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1115Signs of melanoma include a change in the way a mole or pigmented area looks. </h3>

1116<p id="_85" tabindex="-1">

1117These and other <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1118signs</a>

1119 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45022&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045022&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1120symptoms</a>

1121 may be caused by melanoma or by other <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=651193&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000651193&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1122conditions</a>

1123.

1124 Check with your doctor if you have any of the following:</p>

1125<div class="pdq-content-list">

1126<ul id="_86">

1127<li>

1128A mole that:

1129 <div class="pdq-content-list">

1130<ul id="_87" class="list-dash">

1131<li>

1132changes in size, shape, or color.</li>

1133<li>

1134has irregular edges or borders.</li>

1135<li>

1136is more than one color.</li>

1137<li>

1138is <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269454&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269454&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1139asymmetrical</a>

1140 (if the mole is divided in half, the 2

1141 halves are different in size or shape).</li>

1142<li>

1143itches.</li>

1144<li>

1145 oozes, bleeds, or is <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269469&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269469&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1146ulcerated</a>

1147 (a hole forms in the skin when the top layer of cells breaks down and the tissue below shows through).</li>

1148</ul>

1149</div>

1150</li>

1151<li>

1152A change in pigmented (colored) skin.

1153 </li>

1154<li>

1155Satellite moles (new moles that grow near an existing

1156 mole).</li>

1157</ul>

1158</div>

1159<p id="_293" tabindex="-1">

1160For pictures and descriptions of common moles and melanoma, see <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/types/skin/moles-fact-sheet" title="https://www.cancer.gov/types/skin/moles-fact-sheet">

1161Common Moles, Dysplastic Nevi, and Risk of Melanoma</a>

1162.</p>

1164<section id="_88">

1165<h3 id="_89" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1166Tests that examine the skin are used to diagnose melanoma.</h3>

1167<p id="_90" tabindex="-1">

1168In addition to asking about your <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=642019&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000642019&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1169personal</a>

1170 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=642015&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000642015&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1171family health history</a>

1172 and doing a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270871&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270871&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1173physical exam</a>

1174, your doctor may perform the following tests and procedures to find and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046450&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1175diagnose</a>

1176 melanoma:</p>

1177<div class="pdq-content-list">

1178<ul id="_91">

1179<li>

1180<strong>

1181Skin exam</strong>

1182: A doctor or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269445&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269445&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1183nurse</a>

1184 checks the skin for moles, birthmarks, or other pigmented areas that look abnormal in color,

1185 size, shape, or texture.</li>

1186<li>

1187<strong>

1188<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45164&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045164&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1189Biopsy</a>

1190</strong>

1191: A procedure to remove the abnormal tissue and a small amount of normal tissue around it. A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46244&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046244&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1192pathologist</a>

1193 looks at the tissue under a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=638184&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000638184&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1194microscope</a>

1195 to check for cancer cells. It can be hard to tell the difference between a colored mole and an early melanoma <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46324&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046324&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1196lesion</a>

1197. Patients may want to have the sample of tissue checked by a second pathologist. If the abnormal mole or lesion is cancer, the sample of tissue may also be tested for certain gene changes.<p id="_375" tabindex="-1">

1198There are four main types of skin biopsies. The type of biopsy done depends on where the abnormal area formed and the size of the area.</p>

1199<div class="pdq-content-list">

1200<ul id="_376">

1201<li>

1202<strong>

1203<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46578&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046578&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1204Shave biopsy</a>

1205</strong>

1206: A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46600&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046600&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1207sterile</a>

1208 razor blade is used to &#8220;shave-off&#8221; the abnormal-looking growth.</li>

1209<li>

1210<strong>

1211<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=410643&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000410643&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1212Punch biopsy</a>

1213</strong>

1214: A special instrument called a punch or a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=423245&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000423245&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1215trephine</a>

1216 is used to remove a circle of tissue from the abnormal-looking growth.<figure id="figure_145" class="image-center">

1217<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/578083.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1218Enlarge</a>

1219<img id="_145" alt="Punch biopsy; drawing shows a hollow, circular scalpel being inserted into a lesion on the skin of a patient&#8217;s forearm. The instrument is turned clockwise and counterclockwise to cut into the skin and a small sample of tissue is removed to be checked under a microscope. The pullout shows that the instrument cuts down about 4 millimeters (mm) to the layer of fatty tissue below the dermis." title="Punch biopsy; drawing shows a hollow, circular scalpel being inserted into a lesion on the skin of a patient&#8217;s forearm. 1220<figcaption class="caption-container">

1221Punch biopsy. A hollow, circular scalpel is used to cut into a lesion on the skin. A small sample of tissue is removed to be checked under a microscope. Skin thickness is different on different parts of the body.</figcaption>

1222</figure>

1223</li>

1224<li>

1225<strong>

1226<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46698&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046698&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1227Incisional biopsy</a>

1228</strong>

1229: A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=257527&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000257527&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1230scalpel</a>

1231 is used to remove part of a growth.</li>

1232<li>

1233<strong>

1234<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46411&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046411&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1235Excisional biopsy</a>

1236</strong>

1237: A scalpel is used to remove the entire growth.</li>

1238</ul>

1239</div>

1240</li>

1241</ul>

1242</div>

1244<section id="_93">

1245<h3 id="_94" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1246Certain factors affect prognosis (chance of recovery) and treatment options.</h3>

1247<p id="_203" tabindex="-1">

1248The <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45849&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045849&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1249prognosis</a>

1250 and treatment options depend on

1251 the following:</p>

1252<div class="pdq-content-list">

1253<ul id="_191">

1254<li>

1255The thickness of the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1256tumor</a>

1257 and where it is in the body.</li>

1258<li>

1259How quickly the cancer cells are dividing.</li>

1260<li>

1261Whether there was bleeding or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269469&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269469&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1262ulceration</a>

1263 of the tumor.</li>

1264<li>

1265How much cancer is in the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45762&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045762&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1266lymph nodes</a>

1267.</li>

1268<li>

1269The number of places cancer has spread to in the body.</li>

1270<li>

1271 The level of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=354462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000354462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1272lactate dehydrogenase</a>

1273 (LDH) in the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1274blood</a>

1275.</li>

1276<li>

1277Whether the cancer has certain <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46063&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046063&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1278mutations</a>

1279 (changes) in a gene called <em class="gene-name">

1280<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=561325&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000561325&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1281BRAF</a>

1282</em>

1283.</li>

1286 general health.</li>

1296 <section id="_96">

1297

1298 <h2>

1299Stages of Melanoma</h2>

1300

1301 <div id="_section_96" class="pdq-sections">

1302<div class="key-points">

1303<h3 id="_96_kpBoxHdr" do-not-show="toc">

1304Key Points</h3>

1305<div id="_kp_section_96_2">

1306<ul>

1307<li>

1308After melanoma has been diagnosed, tests may be done to find out

1309 if cancer cells have spread within the skin or to other parts of the body.</li>

1310<li>

1311There are three ways that cancer spreads in the body.</li>

1312<li>

1313Cancer may spread from where it began to other parts of the body.</li>

1314<li>

1315The stage of melanoma depends on the thickness of the tumor, whether cancer has spread to lymph nodes or other parts of the body, and other factors. </li>

1316<li>

1317The following stages are used for melanoma:<ul>

1318<li>

1319Stage 0 (Melanoma in Situ) </li>

1320<li>

1321Stage I</li>

1322<li>

1323Stage II </li>

1324<li>

1325Stage III </li>

1326<li>

1327Stage IV </li>

1328</ul>

1329</li>

1330<li>

1331Melanoma can recur

1332 (come back) after it has been treated. </li>

1333</ul>

1334</div>

1337<h3 id="_98" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1338After melanoma has been diagnosed, tests may be done to find out

1339 if cancer cells have spread within the skin or to other parts of the body.</h3>

1340<p id="_99" tabindex="-1">

1341The process used to find out whether <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1342cancer</a>

1343 has spread within the skin or to other parts

1344 of the body is called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46597&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046597&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1345staging</a>

1346. The

1347 information gathered from the staging process determines the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045885&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1348stage</a>

1349 of the

1350 disease. It is important to know the stage in order to plan treatment.

1351 </p>

1352<p id="_100" tabindex="-1">

1353For <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45135&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045135&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1354melanoma</a>

1355 that is not likely to spread to other parts of the body or <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46556&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046556&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1356recur</a>

1357, more tests may not be needed. For melanoma that is likely to spread to other parts of the body or recur, the following tests and procedures may be done after <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45570&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045570&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1373 during surgery. A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46550&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046550&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

A <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46244&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046244&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1443, and a computer to make a series of detailed pictures of areas inside the body, such as the brain. A substance called gadolinium is injected into a vein. 1476<section id="_215">

1477<h3 id="_216" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1478There are three ways that cancer spreads in the body.</h3>

1479<p id="_215_md_69" tabindex="-1">

1480Cancer can spread through <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1481tissue</a>

1482, the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045764&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1483lymph system</a>

1484, and the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1485blood</a>

1486:</p>

1487<div class="pdq-content-list">

1488<ul id="_215_md_70">

1489<li>

1490Tissue. The cancer spreads from where it began by growing into nearby areas.

1491</li>

1492<li>

1493Lymph system. The cancer spreads from where it began by getting into the lymph system. The cancer travels through the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1494lymph vessels</a>

1495 to other parts of the body.

1496</li>

1497<li>

1498Blood. The cancer spreads from where it began by getting into the blood. The cancer travels through the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45020&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045020&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1499blood vessels</a>

1500 to other parts of the body.

1501</li>

1502</ul>

1503</div>

1505<section id="_301">

1506<h3 id="_302" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1507Cancer may spread from where it began to other parts of the body.</h3>

1508<p id="_301_md_66" tabindex="-1">

1509When cancer spreads to another part of the body, it is called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46710&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046710&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1510metastasis</a>

1511. Cancer <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046476&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1512cells</a>

1513 break away from where they began (the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45847&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045847&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1514primary tumor</a>

1515) and travel through the lymph system or blood.</p>

1516<div class="pdq-content-list">

1517<ul id="_301_md_67">

1518<li>

1519Lymph system. The cancer gets into the lymph system, travels through the lymph vessels, and forms a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1520tumor</a>

1521 (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44058&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044058&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1522metastatic</a>

1523 tumor) in another part of the body.</li>

1524<li>

1525Blood. The cancer gets into the blood, travels through the blood vessels, and forms a tumor (metastatic tumor) in another part of the body.</li>

1526</ul>

1527</div>

1528<p id="_303" tabindex="-1">

1529The metastatic tumor is the same type of cancer as the primary tumor. For example, if melanoma spreads to the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270740&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270740&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1530lung</a>

1531, the cancer cells in the lung are actually melanoma cells. The disease is metastatic melanoma, not lung cancer.</p>

1532<div data-embed-button="media_entity_embed" data-entity-embed-display="view_mode:media.video_display_medium_no_title" data-entity-type="media" data-caption="" class="embedded-entity align-center">

1533<figure class="video">

1534<div id="ytplayer-fQwar_-QdiQ" class="flex-video widescreen" data-video-url="https://www.youtube.com/embed/fQwar_-QdiQ?feature=oembed&amp;autoplay=1" data-video-title="metastasis: how cancer spreads">

1535<iframe width="560" height="315" src="https://www.youtube-nocookie.com/embed/fQwar_-QdiQ?rel=0" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" title="metastasis: how cancer spreads" alt="metastasis: how cancer spreads" allowfullscreen="">

1536</iframe>

1537</div>

1538<figcaption class="caption-container">

1539Many cancer deaths are caused when cancer moves from the original tumor and spreads to other tissues and organs. This is called metastatic cancer. This animation shows how cancer cells travel from the place in the body where they first formed to other parts of the body.</figcaption>

1540</figure>

1541</div>

1542</section>

1543<section id="_264">

1544<h3 id="_265" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

1545The stage of melanoma depends on the thickness of the tumor, whether cancer has spread to lymph nodes or other parts of the body, and other factors. </h3>

1546<p id="_340" tabindex="-1">

1547To find out the stage of melanoma, the tumor is completely removed and nearby lymph nodes are checked for <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000750109&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1548signs</a>

1549 of cancer. The stage of the cancer is used to determine which treatment is best. Check with your doctor to find out which stage of cancer you have. </p>

1550<p id="_341" tabindex="-1">

1551The stage of melanoma depends on the following:</p>

1552<div class="pdq-content-list">

1553<ul id="_342">

1554<li>

1555The thickness of the tumor. The thickness of the tumor is measured from the surface of the skin to the deepest part of the tumor.<figure id="figure_377" class="image-center-medium">

1556<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/799465.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1557Enlarge</a>

1558<img id="_377" alt="Melanoma staging (tumor thickness); drawing shows different depths of cancer invasion (0, 1.0, 2.0, 3.0, 4.0, and 5.0 mm) into the epidermis (outer layer of the skin), the dermis (inner layer of the skin), and the subcutaneous tissue below the dermis." title="Melanoma staging (tumor thickness); drawing shows different depths of cancer invasion (0, 1.0, 2.0, 3.0, 4.0, and 5.0 mm) into the epidermis (outer layer of the skin), the dermis (inner layer of the skin), and the subcutaneous tissue below the dermis." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/799465-750.jpg">

1559</figure>

1560</li>

1561<li>

1562Whether the tumor is <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269469&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269469&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1563ulcerated</a>

1564 (has broken through the skin). <figure id="figure_378" class="image-center-medium">

1565<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/799466.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1566Enlarge</a>

1567<img id="_378" alt="Melanoma staging (tumor ulceration); drawing shows a tumor that is ulcerated (has broken through the skin) and a tumor that is not ulcerated." title="Melanoma staging (tumor ulceration); drawing shows a tumor that is ulcerated (has broken through the skin) and a tumor that is not ulcerated." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/799466-750.jpg">

1568</figure>

1569</li>

1570<li>

1571Whether cancer is found in lymph nodes by a physical exam, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=689578&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000689578&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1572imaging tests</a>

1573, or a sentinel lymph node biopsy.<figure id="figure_379" class="image-center-medium">

1574<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/799467.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1575Enlarge</a>

1576<img id="_379" alt="Melanoma staging (lymph node involvement); drawing shows cancer that has spread from the primary tumor to the lymph nodes." title="Melanoma staging (lymph node involvement); drawing shows cancer that has spread from the primary tumor to the lymph nodes." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/799467-750.jpg">

1577</figure>

1578</li>

1579<li>

1580Whether the lymph nodes are <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=793849&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000793849&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1581matted</a>

1582 (joined together). <figure id="figure_380" class="image-center-medium">

1583<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/799461.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1584Enlarge</a>

1585<img id="_380" alt="Melanoma staging (matted lymph nodes); drawing shows matted lymph nodes with cancer." title="Melanoma staging (matted lymph nodes); drawing shows matted lymph nodes with cancer." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/799461-750.jpg">

1586</figure>

1587</li>

1588<li>

1589Whether there are:<div class="pdq-content-list">

1590<ul id="_343">

1591<li>

1592<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=634135&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000634135&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1593Satellite tumors</a>

1594: Small groups of tumor cells that have spread within 2 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=354457&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000354457&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1595centimeters</a>

1596 of the primary tumor.</li>

1597<li>

1598<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=793846&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000793846&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1599Microsatellite tumors</a>

1600: Small groups of tumor cells that have spread to an area right beside or below the primary tumor. </li>

1601<li>

1602<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=634128&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000634128&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1603In-transit metastases</a>

1604: Tumors that have spread to <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=269462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000269462&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1605lymph vessels</a>

1606 in the skin more than 2 centimeters away from the primary tumor, but not to the lymph nodes. </li>

1607</ul>

1608</div>

1609<figure id="figure_381" class="image-center-medium">

1610<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/799462.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1611Enlarge</a>

1612<img id="_381" alt="Melanoma staging (in-transit metastases, satellite tumors, and microsatellite tumors); drawing shows in-transit metastases in a lymph vessel more than 2 centimeters away from the primary tumor and satellite tumors within 2 centimeters of the primary tumor. Microsatellite tumors are not shown because they can only be seen with a microscope." title="Melanoma staging (in-transit metastases, satellite tumors, and microsatellite tumors); drawing shows in-transit metastases in a lymph vessel more than 2 centimeters away from the primary tumor and satellite tumors within 2 centimeters of the primary tumor. Microsatellite tumors are not shown because they can only be seen with a microscope." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/799462-750.jpg">

1613</figure>

1614</li>

1615<li>

1616Whether the cancer has spread to other parts of the body, such as the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270740&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270740&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1617lung</a>

1618, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46312&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046312&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1619liver</a>

1620, brain, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45882&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045882&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1621soft tissue</a>

1622 (including muscle), <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46189&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046189&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1623gastrointestinal tract</a>

1624, and/or distant lymph nodes. Cancer may have spread to places in the skin far away from where it first formed. <figure id="figure_382" class="image-center-medium">

1625<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/799463.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

1626Enlarge</a>

1627<img id="_382" alt="Melanoma staging (cancer spread to other parts of the body); drawing shows cancer cells spreading from the primary cancer, through the blood and lymph system, to another part of the body where a metastatic tumor has formed." title="Melanoma staging (cancer spread to other parts of the body); drawing shows cancer cells spreading from the primary cancer, through the blood and lymph system, to another part of the body where a metastatic tumor has formed." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/799463-750.jpg">

1628</figure>

1629</li>

1630</ul>

1639<p id="_107" tabindex="-1">

1640In <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=352156&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000352156&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1641stage 0</a>

1642, <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44636&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044636&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1643abnormal</a>

1644 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46292&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046292&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1646 are found in the

1647 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46418&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046418&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1649.

1651cancer</a>

1652 and spread into nearby normal <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046683&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1653tissue</a>

1654. Stage 0 is also called <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=522541&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000522541&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1713<p id="_117" tabindex="-1">

1714<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45137&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045137&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1715Stage II</a>

1716 is divided

1717 into stages IIA, IIB, and IIC.</p>

1718<div class="pdq-content-list">

1726

1744 </li>

1746</div>

1747 </li>

1748<li>

1749<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45137&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045137&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1750Stage IIB</a>

1751: The <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046634&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

1752tumor</a>

2076<h3 id="_135_kpBoxHdr" do-not-show="toc">

2077Key Points</h3>

2078<div id="_kp_section_135_3">

2079<ul>

2080<li>

2081There are different types of treatment for patients with

2082 melanoma. </li>

2083<li>

2084The following types of treatment are used:<ul>

2085<li>

2086Surgery </li>

2087<li>

2088Chemotherapy </li>

2089<li>

2090Radiation therapy

2091 </li>

2092<li>

2093Immunotherapy</li>

2094<li>

2095Targeted therapy</li>

2096</ul>

2097</li>

2098<li>

2099New types of treatment are being tested in clinical trials.

2100 <ul>

2101<li>

2102Vaccine therapy</li>

2103</ul>

2104</li>

2105<li>

2106Treatment for melanoma may cause side effects.</li>

2107<li>

2108Patients may want to think about taking part in a clinical trial.</li>

2109<li>

2110Patients can enter clinical trials before, during, or after starting their cancer treatment.</li>

2111<li>

2112Follow-up tests may be needed.</li>

2113</ul>

2118There are different types of treatment for patients with

2119 melanoma. </h3>

2120<p id="_138" tabindex="-1">

2121Different types of treatment are available for patients with

2122 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45135&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045135&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2123melanoma</a>

2124. Some treatments are

2125 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44930&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044930&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2126standard</a>

2127 (the currently used treatment), and some are being tested in

2128 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45961&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045961&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2129clinical trials</a>

2130. A

2131 treatment clinical trial is a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=651211&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000651211&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2132research study</a>

2133 meant to help improve current

2134 treatments or obtain information on new treatments for patients with <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045333&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2135cancer</a>

2136.

2137 When clinical trials show that a new treatment is better than the

2138 standard treatment, the new

2139 treatment may become the standard treatment. Patients may want to think about taking part in a clinical trial. Some clinical trials are open only to patients who have not started treatment.</p>

2220<section id="_148">

2221<h4 id="_149" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

2222Chemotherapy </h4>

2223<p id="_150" tabindex="-1">

2224Chemotherapy is a cancer treatment that uses <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=348921&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000348921&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2225drugs</a>

2226 to stop the growth of cancer cells, either by killing the cells or by stopping them from dividing. When chemotherapy is taken by mouth or injected into a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=476471&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000476471&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2227vein</a>

2228 or muscle, the drugs enter the bloodstream and can reach cancer cells throughout the body (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=301626&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000301626&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2229systemic chemotherapy</a>

2230). When chemotherapy is placed directly into the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46483&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046483&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2231cerebrospinal fluid</a>

2232, an <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=257523&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000257523&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2233organ</a>

2234, or a body <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=463703&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000463703&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2235cavity</a>

2236 such as the <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45070&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045070&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2237abdomen</a>

2238, the drugs mainly affect cancer cells in those areas (<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46559&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046559&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2239regional chemotherapy</a>

2240).</p>

2241<p id="_296" tabindex="-1">

2242One type of regional chemotherapy is <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45716&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045716&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2243hyperthermic</a>

2244 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44853&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044853&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2245isolated limb perfusion</a>

2246. With this method, anticancer drugs go directly to the arm or leg the cancer is in. The flow of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270735&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2247blood</a>

2248 to and from the limb is temporarily stopped with a <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=613900&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000613900&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2249tourniquet</a>

2250. A warm solution with the anticancer drug is put directly into the blood of the limb. This gives a high <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44664&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044664&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2251dose</a>

2252 of drugs to the area where the cancer is.</p>

2253<p id="_204" tabindex="-1">

2254The way the chemotherapy is given depends on the type and stage of the cancer being treated.</p>

2255<p id="_277" tabindex="-1">

2256See <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/drugs/melanoma" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/drugs/melanoma">

2257Drugs Approved for Melanoma</a>

2260<section id="_152">

2261<h4 id="_153" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

2262Radiation therapy

2263 </h4>

2264<p id="_154" tabindex="-1">

2265<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44971&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044971&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2266Radiation therapy</a>

2267 is a cancer treatment that uses high-energy <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045944&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2268x-rays</a>

2269 or other types of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45072&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045072&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2270radiation</a>

2271 to kill cancer cells or keep them from growing. <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46686&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046686&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2272External radiation therapy</a>

2273 uses a machine outside the body to send radiation toward the area of the body with cancer. External radiation therapy is used to treat melanoma and may also be used as <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45815&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045815&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2274palliative therapy</a>

2275 to relieve symptoms and improve quality of life. </p>

2277<section id="_155">

2278<h4 id="_156" type="keypoint" do-not-show="toc">

2279Immunotherapy</h4>

2280<p id="_157" tabindex="-1">

2281<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45729&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045729&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2282Immunotherapy</a>

2283 is a treatment that uses the patient&#8217;s <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46356&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046356&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2284immune system</a>

2285 to fight cancer. Substances made by the body or made in a laboratory are used to boost, direct, or restore the body&#8217;s natural defenses against cancer. </p>

2286<p id="_327" tabindex="-1">

2287The following types of immunotherapy are being used in the treatment of melanoma:</p>

2288<div class="pdq-content-list">

2289<ul id="_319">

2290<li>

2291<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=772606&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000772606&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2292Immune checkpoint inhibitor</a>

2293 <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44737&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044737&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2294therapy</a>

2295: Immune checkpoint inhibitors block <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=46092&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000046092&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2296proteins</a>

2297 called checkpoints that are made by some types of immune system cells, such as <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=44928&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000044928&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2298T cells</a>

2299, and some cancer cells. These checkpoints help keep <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=45722&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000045722&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2300immune responses</a>

2301 from being too strong and sometimes can keep T cells from killing cancer cells. When these checkpoints are blocked, T cells can kill cancer cells better. They are used to treat some patients with <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=478743&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000478743&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2302advanced</a>

2303 melanoma or tumors that cannot be removed by surgery.<p id="_329" tabindex="-1">

2304There are two types of immune checkpoint inhibitor therapy:</p>

2305<div class="pdq-content-list">

2306<ul id="_328">

2307<li>

2308<a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=777030&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000777030&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2309CTLA-4</a>

2310 inhibitor therapy: CTLA-4 is a protein on the surface of T cells that helps keep the body&#8217;s immune responses in check. When CTLA-4 attaches to another protein called B7 on a cancer cell, it stops the T cell from killing the cancer cell. CTLA-4 inhibitors attach to CTLA-4 and allow the T cells to kill cancer cells. <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=535555&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000535555&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2311Ipilimumab</a>

2312 is a type of CTLA-4 inhibitor.<figure id="figure_374" class="image-center">

2313<a href="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/776560.jpg" target="_blank" class="article-image-enlarge">

2314Enlarge</a>

2315<img id="_374" alt="Immune checkpoint inhibitor; the panel on the left shows the binding of the T-cell receptor (TCR) to antigen and MHC proteins on the antigen-presenting cell (APC) and the binding of CD28 on the T cell to B7-1/B7-2 on the APC. It also shows the binding of B7-1/B7-2 to CTLA-4 on the T cell, which keeps the T cells in the inactive state. The panel on the right shows immune checkpoint inhibitor (anti-CTLA antibody) blocking the binding of B7-1/B7-2 to CTLA-4, which allows the T cells to be active and to kill tumor cells." title="Immune checkpoint inhibitor; the panel on the left shows the binding of the T-cell receptor (TCR) to antigen and MHC proteins on the antigen-presenting cell (APC) and the binding of CD28 on the T cell to B7-1/B7-2 on the APC. It also shows the binding of B7-1/B7-2 to CTLA-4 on the T cell, which keeps the T cells in the inactive state. The panel on the right shows immune checkpoint inhibitor (anti-CTLA antibody) blocking the binding of B7-1/B7-2 to CTLA-4, which allows the T cells to be active and to kill tumor cells." src="https://nci-media.cancer.gov/pdq/media/images/776560-750.jpg">

2316<figcaption class="caption-container">

2317Immune checkpoint inhibitor. Checkpoint proteins, such as B7-1/B7-2 on antigen-presenting cells (APC) and CTLA-4 on T cells, help keep the body&#8217;s immune responses in check. When the T-cell receptor (TCR) binds to antigen and major histocompatibility complex (MHC) proteins on the APC and CD28 binds to B7-1/B7-2 on the APC, the T cell can be activated. However, the binding of B7-1/B7-2 to CTLA-4 keeps the T cells in the inactive state so they are not able to kill tumor cells in the body (left panel). Blocking the binding of B7-1/B7-2 to CTLA-4 with an immune checkpoint inhibitor (anti-CTLA-4 antibody) allows the T cells to be active and to kill tumor cells (right panel).</figcaption>

2318</figure>

2319</li>

2322PD-1</a>

2323 and <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=797389&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000797389&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2324PD-L1</a>

2325 inhibitor therapy: PD-1 is a protein on the surface of T cells that helps keep the body&#8217;s immune responses in check. PD-L1 is a protein found on some types of cancer cells. When PD-1 attaches to PD-L1, it stops the T cell from killing the cancer cell. PD-1 and PD-L1 inhibitors keep PD-1 and PD-L1 proteins from attaching to each other. This allows the T cells to kill cancer cells. <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=764538&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000764538&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">

2334vemurafenib</a>

2335 (types of <a class="definition" type="GlossaryTermRefs" href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=270742&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000270742&amp;version=patient&amp;language=English&amp;dictionary=Cancer.gov'); return(false);">
